<p><b>Harry Edward Kane</b> <span class="noexcerpt nowraplinks" style="font-size:85%;"><a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_British_Empire" title="Order of the British Empire">MBE</a></span> (born 28 July 1993) is an English professional <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">footballer</a> who plays as a <a href="/wiki/Striker_(association_football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Striker (association football)">striker</a> for <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> club <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captains</a> the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national team</a>. Regarded as one of the best strikers in the world, Kane is known for his prolific goalscoring record and ability to <a href="/wiki/Playmaker" title="Playmaker">link play</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Born and raised in the London borough of <a href="/wiki/Waltham_Forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Waltham Forest">Waltham Forest</a>, Kane began his career at Tottenham Hotspur, where, after fast progression through the team's youth academy, he was promoted to the senior team in 2009, at age 16. He did not initially feature for the side, and was <a href="/wiki/Loan_(sports)" title="Loan (sports)">loaned</a> out several times to clubs across the <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system" title="English football league system">English football pyramid</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Leyton_Orient_F.C." title="Leyton Orient F.C.">Leyton Orient</a>, <a href="/wiki/Millwall_F.C." title="Millwall F.C.">Millwall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a>. Kane's involvement at Tottenham began to increase following the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Pochettino" title="Mauricio Pochettino">Mauricio Pochettino</a> as head coach in 2014. In his <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2014–15 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">first full season</a> at the club, Kane scored 31 goals across all competitions, was the Premier League's second-highest goalscorer, and was named <a href="/wiki/PFA_Young_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Young Player of the Year">PFA Young Player of the Year</a>.
</p><p>For both the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_Premier_League" title="2015–16 Premier League">2015–16</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League" title="2016–17 Premier League">2016–17</a> seasons, Kane finished as the league's <a href="/wiki/List_of_top_Premier_League_goal_scorers_by_season#2015.E2.80.9316" title="List of top Premier League goal scorers by season">top goalscorer</a>. In the latter season, he helped Tottenham finish as the competition's runners-up and won the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Fans%27_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Fans&#39; Player of the Year">PFA Fans' Player of the Year</a> award. Kane registered his best campaign statistically to date in the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2017–18 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2017–18 season</a>, with 41 goals scored in 48 games across all competitions, and in the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2018–19 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">following season</a>, he finished as a runner-up in the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2019 UEFA Champions League Final">UEFA Champions League</a>. In February 2020, he became Tottenham's second-highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._records_and_statistics#Top_10_all-time_scorers" title="List of Tottenham Hotspur F.C. records and statistics">all-time goalscorer</a> in official competitions.
</p><p>Kane has scored 32 goals in 51 games for England. He appeared and scored at every youth level, and made a goalscoring  debut with the senior team in March 2015, aged 21. Kane featured and scored during England's successful <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying">UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying</a>, and represented the country at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">the tournament itself</a>. He was made the squad's captain from May 2018, prior to the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a>. In that tournament Kane led England to fourth place, their highest finish since <a href="/wiki/1990_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1990 FIFA World Cup">1990</a>. He also finished as the World Cup's top goalscorer, winning the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_awards" title="FIFA World Cup awards">Golden Boot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span></h2>
<p>Kane was born in <a href="/wiki/Walthamstow" title="Walthamstow">Walthamstow</a>, London to Kim (née Hogg) and Patrick Kane and has one older brother, Charlie.<sup id="cite_ref-tottenhamhotspur_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tottenhamhotspur-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-jim_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jim-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> He has Irish ancestry through his father, who is from <a href="/wiki/Galway" title="Galway">Galway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-galway_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-galway-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The family moved to <a href="/wiki/Chingford" title="Chingford">Chingford</a> where Kane attended Larkswood Primary Academy until 2004,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/Chingford_Foundation_School" title="Chingford Foundation School">Chingford Foundation School</a> (also attended by <a href="/wiki/David_Beckham" title="David Beckham">David Beckham</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> He played football from a young age, joining a local club, Ridgeway Rovers, when he was six in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Kane talked about footballing in the family:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I think the sporting genes come from my Mum's side of the family although the topic is a hot debate in the Kane household. Dad probably won't like me saying that, but I think my granddad Eric on my Mum's side was quite a good footballer, and played at a decent level.<sup id="cite_ref-worrall_2_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worrall_2-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Kane also said: "Most of my family were Spurs fans and I grew up 15 minutes from the ground, so I was always going to be a Spurs fan".<sup id="cite_ref-worrall_2_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worrall_2-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> He named former Spurs striker <a href="/wiki/Teddy_Sheringham" title="Teddy Sheringham">Teddy Sheringham</a> his childhood idol, and saw him as a "great finisher" and a role model in his ability to get in the <a href="/wiki/Penalty_area" title="Penalty area">box</a> and score goals.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Other childhood sporting influences he cited include David Beckham and <a href="/wiki/Jermain_Defoe" title="Jermain Defoe">Jermain Defoe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Kane has also spoken of his admiration for the former Brazil forward <a href="/wiki/Ronaldo_(Brazilian_footballer)" title="Ronaldo (Brazilian footballer)">Ronaldo</a>, adding that he loved to watch footage of him on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>: "He was one of the first ones I looked at and thought, 'Wow. He's a goalscorer, I want to be a goalscorer.'"<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_career">Club career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tottenham_Hotspur">Tottenham Hotspur</span></h3>
<h4><span id="2004.E2.80.9310:_Youth_career"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2004–10:_Youth_career">2004–10: Youth career</span></h4>
<p>Kane first played for a local club, Ridgeway Rovers, and joined the <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> youth academy when he was eight years old. He was released after one season for being "a bit chubby" and not "very athletic", according to <a href="/wiki/Liam_Brady" title="Liam Brady">Liam Brady</a> who was then in charge of Arsenal's academy.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Manager <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Arsène Wenger">Arsène Wenger</a> stated in November 2015 that he was disappointed that Arsenal chose to release Kane.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He also had a trial at <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> but was not initially successful,<sup id="cite_ref-worrall_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worrall-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and he returned to his old club Ridgeway Rovers. In 2004, at the age of eleven, he joined <a href="/wiki/Watford_F.C." title="Watford F.C.">Watford</a> academy for a four to six-week trial, and was then given another chance at Tottenham after he impressed playing for Watford against Tottenham.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> He first played at Tottenham as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder" title="Midfielder">midfielder</a> – initially in a holding position, then as an attacking midfielder.<sup id="cite_ref-worrall_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worrall-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In his early days at Tottenham, Kane did not stand out as a player as he was neither big nor was he particularly quick, but those who worked with him noted his constant desire to improve various aspects of his game.<sup id="cite_ref-jim_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jim-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> A couple years after joining, he had a large <a href="/wiki/Growth_spurt" class="mw-redirect" title="Growth spurt">growth spurt</a> that made him taller and physically stronger.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/2008%E2%80%9309_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2008–09 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2008–09 season</a>, he played in the under-16s side that competed in the Copa Chivas tournament in Mexico, and the Bellinzona tournament in Switzerland, scoring three goals.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In July 2009, on his 16th birthday, he signed a scholarship contract with Tottenham.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2009–10 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2009–10 season</a>, Kane played 22 times for Tottenham's under-18s, scoring 18 goals.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Kane appeared on the first-team bench twice during the 2009–10 season.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Both matches were in home domestic cup victories: one the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">League Cup</a> fixture against <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a> on 27 October 2009<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> and the other in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> fourth-round <a href="/wiki/Replay_(sports)" title="Replay (sports)">replay</a> against <a href="/wiki/Bolton_Wanderers_F.C." title="Bolton Wanderers F.C.">Bolton Wanderers</a> on 24 February 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> He signed his first professional contract with the club in July 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2011.E2.80.9314:_Loan_spells_across_England"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2011–14:_Loan_spells_across_England">2011–14: Loan spells across England</span></h4>
<p>On 7 January 2011, Kane moved to <a href="/wiki/Leyton_Orient_F.C." title="Leyton Orient F.C.">Leyton Orient</a> on <a href="/wiki/Loan_(sports)" title="Loan (sports)">loan</a> until the end of the <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_Leyton_Orient_F.C._season" title="2010–11 Leyton Orient F.C. season">2010–11 season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Manager <a href="/wiki/Russell_Slade" title="Russell Slade">Russell Slade</a> was "happy" at his arrival and said, "I'm sure he will have an impact with us over the coming months".<sup id="cite_ref-Harry_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harry-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> He made his first-team debut for Orient on 15 January, coming on as a <a href="/wiki/Substitute_(association_football)" title="Substitute (association football)">substitute</a> for <a href="/wiki/Scott_McGleish" title="Scott McGleish">Scott McGleish</a> in the 73rd minute of a 1–1 draw away to <a href="/wiki/Rochdale_A.F.C." title="Rochdale A.F.C.">Rochdale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> A week later, Kane scored his first first-team goal against <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a>; making his first-ever start, "unmarked" Kane scored from a <a href="/wiki/Dean_Cox_(English_footballer)" title="Dean Cox (English footballer)">Dean Cox</a> freekick in the 57th minute as Orient eventually won 4–0.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Slade said that he was "delighted" that Kane scored a goal on his first league start.<sup id="cite_ref-Harry_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harry-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> On 12 February, he scored twice in a 4–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Rovers_F.C." title="Bristol Rovers F.C.">Bristol Rovers</a>, after coming on as a substitute for McGleish in the 70th minute.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> He ended the season scoring five goals in 18 matches.<sup id="cite_ref-Kane_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kane-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 August 2011, Kane made his first appearance for Tottenham, starting in the second leg of their <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> qualification round against <a href="/wiki/Heart_of_Midlothian_F.C." title="Heart of Midlothian F.C.">Hearts</a>, with Tottenham making changes after winning the first leg 5–0. His debut was a goalless match, although he won a <a href="/wiki/Penalty_kick_(association_football)" title="Penalty kick (association football)">penalty</a> after being fouled by goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Jamie_MacDonald_(footballer)" title="Jamie MacDonald (footballer)">Jamie MacDonald</a>, who then saved the penalty which Kane took himself.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> He went on to make six appearances in the Europa League <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2011–12 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">that season</a>, scoring his first Tottenham goal in the 4–0 win away to <a href="/wiki/Shamrock_Rovers_F.C." title="Shamrock Rovers F.C.">Shamrock Rovers</a> on 15 December 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 29 December 2011, Kane and Tottenham teammate <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Mason" title="Ryan Mason">Ryan Mason</a> agreed to join <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a> club <a href="/wiki/Millwall_F.C." title="Millwall F.C.">Millwall</a> on loan from 1 January 2012 until the end of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> After making his debut against <a href="/wiki/Bristol_City_F.C." title="Bristol City F.C.">Bristol City</a>, manager <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Jackett" title="Kenny Jackett">Kenny Jackett</a> said that he had "very good debut" but was "unlucky not to score". He also said that Kane would "be a good addition" for the club in the second half of the season. He went on to score seven goals in the final 14 matches of the season.<sup id="cite_ref-Harry_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harry-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Kane scored nine goals in 27 matches which resulted in him being named Millwall's Young Player of the Year for <a href="/wiki/2011%E2%80%9312_Millwall_F.C._season" title="2011–12 Millwall F.C. season">2011–12</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-YPOTY_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YPOTY-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> His run of goals scored towards the end of the season has been credited with helping to raise Millwall in the table away from the threat of relegation that season.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kane spent pre-season 2012–13 season with Tottenham, scoring a <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick#Association_football" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> in a 6–0 away win against <a href="/wiki/Southend_United_F.C." title="Southend United F.C.">Southend United</a> on 10 August 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On 18 August, he made his <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Premier_League" title="2012–13 Premier League">Premier League</a> debut, against <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_United_F.C." title="Newcastle United F.C.">Newcastle United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Coming as an 86th-minute substitute for <a href="/wiki/Sandro_(footballer,_born_1989)" title="Sandro (footballer, born 1989)">Sandro</a>, Tottenham lost 2–1.<sup id="cite_ref-Harry_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harry-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 31 August 2012, Kane joined Premier League team <a href="/wiki/Norwich_City_F.C." title="Norwich City F.C.">Norwich City</a> on a season-long loan,<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> making his debut as a substitute against <a href="/wiki/West_Ham_United_F.C." title="West Ham United F.C.">West Ham United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Kane suffered an injury, breaking a <a href="/wiki/Metatarsal_bone" class="mw-redirect" title="Metatarsal bone">metatarsal bone</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Football_League_Cup" title="2012–13 Football League Cup">League Cup</a> tie against <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Rovers_F.C." title="Doncaster Rovers F.C.">Doncaster Rovers</a> in only his second appearance.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The 19-year-old underwent his rehabilitation at Tottenham but returned to action for Norwich on 29 December 2012, coming off the bench at half time as Norwich lost 3–4 to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> However, with Tottenham having been unable to add to their attacking options during the January transfer window, they opted to recall Kane on 1 February 2013, four months before he was due to return.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Twenty days after he was recalled to Tottenham, Kane joined <a href="/wiki/Leicester_City_F.C." title="Leicester City F.C.">Leicester City</a> for the remainder of the season to aid in the club's push for automatic promotion from the Championship.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> He marked his home debut with a goal against <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a>, in a 3–0 win on 26 February 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> He made 13 appearances for the <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands" title="East Midlands">East Midlands</a> club, eight from the bench, and they reached <a href="/wiki/2013_Football_League_play-offs#Champonship" title="2013 Football League play-offs">the play-off semi-final</a> before being eliminated by Watford.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kane scored his first Tottenham goal of the 2013–14 season at <a href="/wiki/White_Hart_Lane" title="White Hart Lane">White Hart Lane</a> in a <a href="/wiki/2013%E2%80%9314_Football_League_Cup" title="2013–14 Football League Cup">League Cup</a> tie against <a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a>, scoring the equaliser in extra time, the match finished 2–2.<sup id="cite_ref-Hull_City_League_Cup_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hull_City_League_Cup-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Tottenham won 8–7 on <a href="/wiki/Penalty_shoot-out_(association_football)" title="Penalty shoot-out (association football)">penalties</a>, with Kane taking and converting the fifth of the nine sets of spot-kicks.<sup id="cite_ref-Hull_City_League_Cup_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hull_City_League_Cup-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 7 April 2014, Kane was given his first Premier League start for Tottenham, in a 5–1 win against <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a>, and scored his first Premier League goal in the 59th minute.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> He also scored in the following match, helping Tottenham to recover from a 3–0 deficit against <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a> before eventually drawing 3–3.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> He scored for the third match in a row on 19 April, this time helping Tottenham to a 3–1 <a href="/wiki/London_derbies" title="London derbies">London derby</a> win at home over <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2014.E2.80.9315_season:_PFA_Young_Player_of_the_Year"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014–15_season:_PFA_Young_Player_of_the_Year">2014–15 season: PFA Young Player of the Year</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spurs_5_Chelsea_3_(16175596592).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Spurs_5_Chelsea_3_%2816175596592%29.jpg/220px-Spurs_5_Chelsea_3_%2816175596592%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Spurs_5_Chelsea_3_%2816175596592%29.jpg/330px-Spurs_5_Chelsea_3_%2816175596592%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Spurs_5_Chelsea_3_%2816175596592%29.jpg/440px-Spurs_5_Chelsea_3_%2816175596592%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2827" data-file-height="2827" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spurs_5_Chelsea_3_(16175596592).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kane (left) playing for <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> against Chelsea in 2015. Kane scored twice in a 5–3 Spurs win.<sup id="cite_ref-Spurs_Chelsea_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spurs_Chelsea-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>Kane made his first appearance of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2014–15 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2014–15 season</a> as a substitute against West Ham on the opening day of the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Premier_League" title="2014–15 Premier League">Premier League season</a>, providing an assist for the match-winning goal by <a href="/wiki/Eric_Dier" title="Eric Dier">Eric Dier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> He scored in both matches against Cypriot opposition <a href="/wiki/AEL_Limassol" title="AEL Limassol">AEL Limassol</a> in Tottenham's <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2014–15 UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League play-offs</a>, scoring an 80th-minute winner in the first leg, and opening the scoring in the 3–0 second leg victory after missing a penalty.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> He scored a late goal against <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_Forest_F.C." title="Nottingham Forest F.C.">Nottingham Forest</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9315_Football_League_Cup" title="2014–15 Football League Cup">League Cup</a> to secure a 3–1 victory for Tottenham on 24 September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> On 23 October 2014, Kane scored his first professional hat-trick for Tottenham in a 5–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Asteras_Tripoli_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Asteras Tripoli F.C.">Asteras Tripoli</a> in the group stage of the UEFA Europa League.<sup id="cite_ref-Asteras_Tripoli_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asteras_Tripoli-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Kane was forced to play <a href="/wiki/Goalkeeper_(association_football)" title="Goalkeeper (association football)">in goal</a> for the final three minutes, after <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Lloris" title="Hugo Lloris">Hugo Lloris</a> had been sent off with no substitutions remaining, and conceded a goal when he dropped a free-kick from <a href="/wiki/Jer%C3%B3nimo_Barrales" title="Jerónimo Barrales">Jerónimo Barrales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Asteras_Tripoli_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asteras_Tripoli-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 November 2014, Kane came on as a second-half substitute in Tottenham's 2–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a> and scored his first Premier League goal of the season to win the match in the 90th minute.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> A week later, Kane was selected in Spurs' starting line-up for the first time in the Premier League season, as the team lost 2–1 at home to <a href="/wiki/Stoke_City_F.C." title="Stoke City F.C.">Stoke City</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> He retained his place in the first XI for Spurs' 2–1 win away to Hull City on 23 November, scoring the team's equalising goal.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Between 14 and 26 December, Kane scored in three consecutive 2–1 wins for Tottenham, against <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Burnley_F.C." title="Burnley F.C.">Burnley</a><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> and Leicester City<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> respectively. On 1 January 2015, Kane scored twice and won a penalty as Tottenham defeated <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C.%E2%80%93Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._rivalry" title="Chelsea F.C.–Tottenham Hotspur F.C. rivalry">rivals</a> and league leaders <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> 5–3,<sup id="cite_ref-Spurs_Chelsea_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spurs_Chelsea-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and he scored a further two in a 3–0 away win against West Bromwich Albion on 31 January, including one from a penalty.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Kane set up <a href="/wiki/Christian_Eriksen" title="Christian Eriksen">Christian Eriksen</a>'s late equaliser against <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a> on 28 January 2015, a goal which put Tottenham into the <a href="/wiki/2015_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2015 Football League Cup Final">2015 League Cup Final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> His performances led to him being named as the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Player_of_the_Month" title="Premier League Player of the Month">Premier League Player of the Month</a> for January 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-PremProfile_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PremProfile-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 February 2015, Kane signed a new five-and-a-half-year contract with the club.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Five days later, he scored both of Tottenham's goals as they came from behind to defeat Arsenal in the <a href="/wiki/North_London_derby" title="North London derby">North London derby</a>, his 21st and 22nd goals of the season across all competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> After scoring against Arsenal, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a> and West Ham United, Kane was again named as the Premier League Player of the Month for February 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-PremProfile_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PremProfile-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> becoming only the fourth player to win the award in consecutive months.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Tottenham lost the League Cup Final 2–0 to rivals Chelsea on 1 March 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-2015LC_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015LC-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> which Kane described as the "worst feeling in the world".<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Twenty days later, he scored his first <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premier_League_hat-tricks" title="List of Premier League hat-tricks">Premier League hat-trick</a> in a 4–3 home win over his former loan club Leicester;<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> this brought him to 19 league goals in the season, making him the division's top scorer.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 5 April, Kane <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captained</a> Tottenham for the first time in a 0–0 draw with Burnley at <a href="/wiki/Turf_Moor" title="Turf Moor">Turf Moor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Two weeks later, he scored his 30th goal of the season in a 3–1 win against Newcastle United at <a href="/wiki/St_James%27_Park" title="St James&#39; Park">St James' Park</a>, making him the first Tottenham player to reach that milestone since <a href="/wiki/Gary_Lineker" title="Gary Lineker">Gary Lineker</a> in <a href="/wiki/1991%E2%80%9392_Football_League" title="1991–92 Football League">1991–92</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Later that month, he was included as one of two forwards in the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Team_of_the_Year" title="PFA Team of the Year">PFA Team of the Year</a>, alongside Chelsea's <a href="/wiki/Diego_Costa" title="Diego Costa">Diego Costa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-PFA1415_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFA1415-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> He was also voted the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Young_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Young Player of the Year">PFA Young Player of the Year</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-young_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-young-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> On 24 May 2015, he headed in an Eric Dier cross for the only goal of an away win over Everton on the final day of the season to confirm fifth place for Tottenham, thus qualifying them to the group stage of the following season's UEFA Europa League. It was his 21st goal of the league campaign, equalling a Premier League club record alongside Teddy Sheringham, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Klinsmann" title="Jürgen Klinsmann">Jürgen Klinsmann</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Bale" title="Gareth Bale">Gareth Bale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> At the end of the season, Kane remarked that he had done more in the single campaign than he had expected to do in his whole career.<sup id="cite_ref-stuff_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stuff-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2015.E2.80.9316_season:_Premier_League_top_goalscorer"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2015–16_season:_Premier_League_top_goalscorer">2015–16 season: Premier League top goalscorer</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harry_Kane_(24685589756).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Harry_Kane_%2824685589756%29.jpg/220px-Harry_Kane_%2824685589756%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Harry_Kane_%2824685589756%29.jpg/330px-Harry_Kane_%2824685589756%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Harry_Kane_%2824685589756%29.jpg/440px-Harry_Kane_%2824685589756%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3193" data-file-height="2408" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harry_Kane_(24685589756).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kane captaining Spurs in 2016. He inherited the number 10 jersey at the start of the 2015–16 season</div></div></div>
<p>On Tottenham's pre-season tour of Australia, Kane attracted numerous fans while visiting the <a href="/wiki/Westfield_Sydney" title="Westfield Sydney">Westfield Sydney</a> shopping centre, resulting in the club sending a minibus to escort him away.<sup id="cite_ref-stuff_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stuff-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> On 29 July 2015, Tottenham were the guests in the <a href="/wiki/2015_MLS_All-Star_Game" title="2015 MLS All-Star Game">2015 MLS All-Star Game</a> at <a href="/wiki/Dick%27s_Sporting_Goods_Park" title="Dick&#39;s Sporting Goods Park">Dick's Sporting Goods Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Commerce_City,_Colorado" title="Commerce City, Colorado">Commerce City, Colorado</a>. They lost 2–1 to the MLS All-Stars, with Kane scoring their consolation goal in the 37th minute after beating a challenge from <a href="/wiki/Omar_Gonzalez" title="Omar Gonzalez">Omar Gonzalez</a>, and he was later substituted in the 77th minute.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kane's squad number was changed from 18 to 10, previously worn by <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Adebayor" title="Emmanuel Adebayor">Emmanuel Adebayor</a>. In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i>, he said that he changed the number "to become a club legend".<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> With Adebayor and <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Soldado" title="Roberto Soldado">Roberto Soldado</a> having been put up for sale, he began the season as the club's only forward, and the third-choice captain behind Hugo Lloris and <a href="/wiki/Jan_Vertonghen" title="Jan Vertonghen">Jan Vertonghen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-stuff_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stuff-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> After a 748-minute drought, he scored his first goal of the season on 26 September 2015 as Tottenham came from behind to defeat leaders Manchester City 4–1.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Eight days later, he scored an <a href="/wiki/Own_goal" title="Own goal">own goal</a> from <a href="/wiki/Jonjo_Shelvey" title="Jonjo Shelvey">Jonjo Shelvey</a>'s corner kick away to Swansea City, but Tottenham fought back to a 2–2 draw.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 October 2015, Kane scored a hat-trick, including a penalty which he won himself, as Tottenham came from conceding a first-minute goal to triumph 5–1 away to <a href="/wiki/A.F.C._Bournemouth" class="mw-redirect" title="A.F.C. Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a> at <a href="/wiki/Dean_Court" title="Dean Court">Dean Court</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Eight days later, he recorded his fifth goal of the season with the final goal in a 3–1 win at home to Aston Villa.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> On 8 November 2015, he gave Tottenham a half-time lead against Arsenal at the <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Stadium" title="Emirates Stadium">Emirates Stadium</a>, albeit in a 1–1 draw;<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> this goal past <a href="/wiki/Petr_%C4%8Cech" title="Petr ech">Petr ech</a> was from his first touch of <a href="/wiki/Danny_Rose_(footballer,_born_1990)" title="Danny Rose (footballer, born 1990)">Danny Rose</a>'s long pass.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Eighteen days after that, he recorded his ninth goal in six matches, the only one of an away match against <a href="/wiki/Qaraba%C4%9F_FK" title="Qaraba FK">Qaraba FK</a>, qualifying Tottenham to the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Europa_League_knockout_phase" title="2015–16 UEFA Europa League knockout phase">knockout stages</a> of <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2015–16 UEFA Europa League">the season's UEFA Europa League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> On 19 December 2015, Kane made his 100th appearance for the club in a 2–0 win away to <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a>, and scored his 10th goal in his last 10 matches.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> A week later, he added two more in a 3–0 win over former loan employers Norwich, putting him on 27 Premier League goals for the year 2015, breaking Sheringham's club record.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> On 10 January 2016, he scored his 50th goal for Tottenham in a 2–2 draw against Leicester in the third round of the <a href="/wiki/2015%E2%80%9316_FA_Cup" title="2015–16 FA Cup">FA Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kane was Premier League Player of the Month for the third time in March 2016, after scoring five goals in four games, including one in the North London derby.<sup id="cite_ref-PremProfile_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PremProfile-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> After scoring his 22nd league goal of the season in a 1–1 draw against Liverpool at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a> on 2 April, Kane became the club's highest goalscorer in a single Premier League season, with six games of the season remaining.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kane ended the season winning the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League_Golden_Boot" title="Premier League Golden Boot">Premier League Golden Boot</a>, finishing one goal ahead of <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Ag%C3%BCero" title="Sergio Agüero">Sergio Agüero</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Vardy" title="Jamie Vardy">Jamie Vardy</a> with 25 goals.<sup id="cite_ref-golden_boot_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golden_boot-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> He was named in the PFA Team of the Year for the second consecutive season,<sup id="cite_ref-PFA1516_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFA1516-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> as he helped Tottenham to a third-place finish, and <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2016–17 UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> qualification.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2016.E2.80.9317_season:_League_runner-up_and_second_Golden_Boot"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2016–17_season:_League_runner-up_and_second_Golden_Boot">2016–17 season: League runner-up and second Golden Boot</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_United_v_Tottenham_Hotspur,_December_2016_(08).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Manchester_United_v_Tottenham_Hotspur%2C_December_2016_%2808%29.JPG/220px-Manchester_United_v_Tottenham_Hotspur%2C_December_2016_%2808%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Manchester_United_v_Tottenham_Hotspur%2C_December_2016_%2808%29.JPG/330px-Manchester_United_v_Tottenham_Hotspur%2C_December_2016_%2808%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Manchester_United_v_Tottenham_Hotspur%2C_December_2016_%2808%29.JPG/440px-Manchester_United_v_Tottenham_Hotspur%2C_December_2016_%2808%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_United_v_Tottenham_Hotspur,_December_2016_(08).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kane (centre) with his Spurs teammates before a Premier League game against <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> in December 2016</div></div></div>
<p>In the absence of <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Lloris" title="Hugo Lloris">Hugo Lloris</a>, Kane captained Tottenham in their opening home match of the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2016–17 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2016–17 season</a>, assisting <a href="/wiki/Victor_Wanyama" title="Victor Wanyama">Victor Wanyama</a>'s winning goal as Spurs beat <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Palace_F.C." title="Crystal Palace F.C.">Crystal Palace</a> 1–0 in a London derby at White Hart Lane.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> He opened his scoring account in the fourth matchday of the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Premier_League" title="2016–17 Premier League">Premier League season</a>, providing the final goal in a 4–0 win away to Stoke City.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 September 2016, Kane made his <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> debut in Spurs' 2–1 loss to <a href="/wiki/AS_Monaco_FC" title="AS Monaco FC">Monaco</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium" title="Wembley Stadium">Wembley Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Four days later, he scored the winning goal against Sunderland in the Premier League, but had to be helped off the field after twisting his right ankle attempting a tackle of <a href="/wiki/Papy_Djilobodji" title="Papy Djilobodji">Papy Djilobodji</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Reports indicated that the ligaments in Kane's ankle were damaged, ruling him out for six-to-eight weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> After missing five league matches and three in the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_UEFA_Champions_League#Group_E" title="2016–17 UEFA Champions League">Champions League group phase</a>, Kane made his return at rivals Arsenal on 6 November, scoring from the penalty spot to equalise in a 1–1 draw.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> On 22 November, he scored his first Champions League goal in the return fixture against Monaco at the <a href="/wiki/Stade_Louis_II" title="Stade Louis II">Stade Louis II</a>, a game which saw Spurs eliminated from the competition with a 2–1 loss.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 December 2016, Kane signed a new contract with Tottenham, keeping him at the club until 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> On 1 January 2017, made his 100th Premier League appearance,<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> scoring the first Premier League goal of the new year against Watford on the 27-minute mark, which he extended to a brace after scoring again in the 33rd minute.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> In his first match after the birth of his daughter, Kane scored a hat-trick in a 4–0 win against West Brom on 14 January.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In the fifth round of the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_FA_Cup" title="2016–17 FA Cup">2016–17 FA Cup</a> on 19 February 2017, Kane scored all three goals as Tottenham beat Fulham 3–0. This meant his fifth career hat-trick, and his second in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> On 26 February 2017, Kane once again scored a hat-trick as Tottenham beat Stoke 4–0, his third hat-trick in nine games, and his second in consecutive domestic games.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The first of these goals was his 100th in club football.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> He was named Player of the Month for the fourth time in his career in February 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-PremProfile_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PremProfile-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2017, he injured his ankle in an FA Cup match against former loan club Millwall.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> On 15 April, Kane scored his 20th Premier League goal of the season against Bournemouth on his first start in a month after returning from injury. This made him the fourth player in Premier League history to achieve 20 goals in three consecutive seasons, after <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thierry_Henry" title="Thierry Henry">Thierry Henry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ruud_van_Nistelrooy" title="Ruud van Nistelrooy">Ruud van Nistelrooy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 April, Kane was named in the PFA Team of the Year for the third consecutive season.<sup id="cite_ref-PFA1617_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFA1617-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> He was also included in the six player shortlists for the <a href="/wiki/PFA_Players%27_Player_of_the_Year" title="PFA Players&#39; Player of the Year">PFA Players' Player of the Year</a> and PFA Young Player of the Year awards.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Two days later, he scored in Tottenham's 4–2 <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_semi-finals" title="FA Cup semi-finals">FA Cup semi-final</a> loss to rivals Chelsea at Wembley Stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> In the last match at White Hart Lane on 14 May, Harry Kane scored the 2–0 goal as Tottenham beat <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> 2–1.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> With two games remaining of the season, Kane stood on 22 goals, two fewer than <a href="/wiki/Romelu_Lukaku" title="Romelu Lukaku">Romelu Lukaku</a>. With a combined seven goals in the last two fixtures however, a 6–1 win over reigning champions Leicester City<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> and a 7–1 win against Hull City,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Kane finished as the top scorer of the Premier League on 29 goals, and thus won his second consecutive Golden Boot, becoming only the fifth player to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-golden_boot_2017_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-golden_boot_2017-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2017.E2.80.9318_season:_Record_breaking_year"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–18_season:_Record_breaking_year">2017–18 season: Record breaking year</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harry_Kane_(35805453874).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Harry_Kane_%2835805453874%29.jpg/220px-Harry_Kane_%2835805453874%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Harry_Kane_%2835805453874%29.jpg/330px-Harry_Kane_%2835805453874%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Harry_Kane_%2835805453874%29.jpg/440px-Harry_Kane_%2835805453874%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4912" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harry_Kane_(35805453874).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kane during a pre-season game for Spurs at <a href="/wiki/Nissan_Stadium" title="Nissan Stadium">Nissan Stadium</a> in Nashville, Tennessee, July 2017</div></div></div>
<p>After not finding the back of the net in Tottenham's first three games, Kane scored a brace in three of his next four appearances for the club across all competitions.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> His opening goal against Everton on 9 September was his 100th overall for the club, coming in his 169th appearance.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> On 26 September, Kane scored his first <a href="/wiki/List_of_UEFA_Champions_League_hat-tricks" title="List of UEFA Champions League hat-tricks">UEFA Champions League hat-trick</a> in a 3–0 <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_UEFA_Champions_League_group_stage" title="2017–18 UEFA Champions League group stage">group stage</a> win against Cypriot champions <a href="/wiki/APOEL_FC" title="APOEL FC">APOEL</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> He was awarded Premier League Player of the Month for the fifth time, and named September 2017 – in which he scored 13 goals in 10 club and international games – as the best month of his career.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:25%; ;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1012376600">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">I think he is in that level, with Batistuta, I would put Harry Kane in with Batistuta. Yes, yes, yes, yes – Batistuta was a killer. And very strong mentality, very strong shot, great professional, I think yes, you can compare.</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— Pochettino compares Kane with <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Batistuta" title="Gabriel Batistuta">Gabriel Batistuta</a>, September 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>On 23 December, Kane equalled Alan Shearer's record of 36 Premier League goals in a calendar year, having scored a hat-trick in a 0–3 away win to Burnley.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> He surpassed Shearer's record the following game with another hat-trick in the 5–2 home win against Southampton, ending the year with 39 Premier League goals.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The hat-trick, his sixth of the year in the Premier League (eighth in all competitions), also made him the first player in Premier League history to score six hat-tricks in a year.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> With a total of 56 goals scored in all competitions for the year, he also became Europe's top goal scorer of 2017, breaking the seven-year dominance of <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">Lionel Messi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a> as Europe's top goalscorer in a calendar year.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2018, he scored twice in the 4–0 home win against Everton, and became Tottenham's top goalscorer in the Premier League era, breaking Teddy Sheringham's record of 97 Premier League goals for the club.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> On 4 February, Kane scored an added-time penalty to equalise in a 2–2 draw with Liverpool at <a href="/wiki/Anfield" title="Anfield">Anfield</a> for his <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premier_League_players_with_100_or_more_goals" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Premier League players with 100 or more goals">100th Premier League goal</a>; he achieved the century of league goals in 141 games, beaten only by <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a>'s 124.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> He was named in the PFA Team of the Year for the fourth consecutive season in April 2018, alongside fellow forwards <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Salah" title="Mohamed Salah">Mohamed Salah</a> and Sergio Agüero.<sup id="cite_ref-PFA1718_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PFA1718-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> On 8 June, Kane signed a new contract to keep him at the club until 2024.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2018.E2.80.932020:_UEFA_Champions_League_runner-up_and_injuries"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–2020:_UEFA_Champions_League_runner-up_and_injuries">2018–2020: UEFA Champions League runner-up and injuries</span></h4>
<p>Kane started the season opener against Newcastle United without scoring, before opening his account against <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a> the following weekend. In doing so he ended his hoodoo of failing to score a Premier League goal in the month of August.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> He also scored for the first time at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> in the following game as Tottenham won 3–0 in what was only their third away win against Manchester United since 1992, as well as the biggest away win against the club in 46 years.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> He scored the opening goal against <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff</a> on 1 January 2019, and with that goal, he became the first player to have scored a goal against every Premier League team he has faced.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> On 13 January 2019, in a match against Manchester United, Kane injured his ankle ligaments late in the game, thereby missing some crucial games including the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2018–19 UEFA Champions League">Champions League</a> last-16 home game.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He returned to the first team squad on 23 February 2019, in a match against Burnley, and was immediately placed in the starting XI. He scored the equalizing goal in the 65th minute to tie the score 1–1, although the match ended a 1–2 defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> He scored the only goal in the Champions League last-16 away tie against Borussia Dortmund to ensure a 4–0 win on aggregate and progress to the club's second quarter-final in the Champions League. The goal also made him the club's top goalscorer in European competitions with 24 goals scored.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> During the first leg of the quarter-final in the Champions League on 9 April 2019 against Manchester City, he again suffered an ankle injury, which ended his season domestically in the Premier League.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> He did, however, return for the <a href="/wiki/2019_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2019 UEFA Champions League Final">Champions League final</a> on 1 June 2019, although his selection after his injury became a subject of debate as Tottenham lost 2–0 to Liverpool.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kane started Tottenham's first game of the <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2019–20 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2019–20 season</a>, scoring twice in a 3–1 home win against <a href="/wiki/Aston_Villa_F.C." title="Aston Villa F.C.">Aston Villa</a>. Kane's first goal of the game was his first at the <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_Stadium" title="Tottenham Hotspur Stadium">Tottenham Hotspur Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> On 1 January 2020, in the away match against Southampton that ended in a 1–0 defeat, Kane suffered a hamstring injury.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The damage to his hamstring required an operation which would see him out of action for a few months.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> which resulted in the suspension of League matches, he did not play any further matches until 19 June.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> On 23 June, in his 200th Premier League appearance for Tottenham, he scored his first goal of 2020 against West Ham, sealing a 2–0 win.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2020.E2.80.9321_season"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2020–21_season">2020–21 season</span></h4>
<p>Kane scored his first goal of the season in the <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_UEFA_Europa_League" title="2020–21 UEFA Europa League">Europa League</a> match against <a href="/wiki/PFC_Lokomotiv_Plovdiv" title="PFC Lokomotiv Plovdiv">Lokomotiv Plovdiv</a>, helping the team to win 2–1 after Plovdiv had two players sent off late in the second half.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> His first league goal of the <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2020–21 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2020–21 season</a> came in the second league match following a spree of four goals which were all scored by <a href="/wiki/Son_Heung-min" title="Son Heung-min">Son Heung-min</a> and assisted by Kane, giving Spurs a 5–2 win over Southampton. This is the first time in Premier League history a player has provided four assists to the same teammate in a match and Kane became just the sixth player in Premier League history to assist four goals in a single match, and the first English player to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kane scored a hat-trick against <a href="/wiki/Maccabi_Haifa_F.C." title="Maccabi Haifa F.C.">Maccabi Haifa</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_UEFA_Europa_League_qualifying_phase_and_play-off_round#Play-off_round" title="2020–21 UEFA Europa League qualifying phase and play-off round">UEFA Europa League play-off</a> round on 1 October, securing qualification for the group stage.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> On 4 October, he scored a brace in a 6–1 away win against Manchester United, which is the biggest win for Tottenham at <a href="/wiki/Old_Trafford" title="Old Trafford">Old Trafford</a> and their best result against United since a home win in 1932.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> He scored his 200th goal for Tottenham in his 300th appearance for the club in the 3–1 win over <a href="/wiki/PFC_Ludogorets_Razgrad" title="PFC Ludogorets Razgrad">Ludogorets</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2020%E2%80%9321_UEFA_Europa_League_group_stage" title="2020–21 UEFA Europa League group stage">group stage</a> of the Europa League.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Kane scored in Tottenham's 2–0 victory over rivals Arsenal making him the record highest goalscorer in the history of the North London Derby with 11 goals.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> It was also Kane's 100th home goal for Tottenham in all competitions, and his 250th career goal for club and country.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 2 January 2021, Kane converted a penalty to open the scoring and later provided an assist during Tottenham's 3-0 home victory over <a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a>. This brought both Kane's goal and assist tally in the league to 10, making him the first player in Europe's top five leagues to reach double digits for goals and assists in the 2020-21 season.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> On 7 March, he scored a brace against Crystal Palace in a 4–1 win; the last goal was assisted by Son Heung-min, and this, their 14th combined goal effort whereby one assisted another, set a record for the most goal combinations in a Premier League season.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_career">International career</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Youth">Youth</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Harry_Kane.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Harry_Kane.jpg/170px-Harry_Kane.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="264" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Harry_Kane.jpg/255px-Harry_Kane.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Harry_Kane.jpg/340px-Harry_Kane.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1934" data-file-height="2998" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Harry_Kane.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kane warming up for England at the <a href="/wiki/2012_UEFA_European_Under-19_Championship" title="2012 UEFA European Under-19 Championship">2012 UEFA European Under-19 Championship</a></div></div></div>
<p>In January 2010, Kane was called up to play for the <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-17_football_team" title="England national under-17 football team">England under-17 team</a> for the Algarve Tournament in Portugal.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Kane missed the <a href="/wiki/2010_UEFA_European_Under-17_Championship" title="2010 UEFA European Under-17 Championship">2010 UEFA European Under-17 Championship</a> due to illness, with England going on to win the tournament in his absence.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> He later moved up to the <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-19_football_team" title="England national under-19 football team">under-19s</a> and scored twice in a 6–1 victory over <a href="/wiki/Albania_national_under-19_football_team" title="Albania national under-19 football team">Albania</a> on 8 October 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Kane played a large role in the England under-19s progression to the semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2012_UEFA_European_Under-19_Championship" title="2012 UEFA European Under-19 Championship">2012 UEFA European Under-19 Championship</a> in Estonia. Kane scored the winner against France in the final group stage match to ensure the team a safe passage through to the semi-finals.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> In total Kane appeared 14 times for England U19s and contributed 6 goals during that period.<sup id="cite_ref-FA_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FA-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 28 May 2013, he was named in manager <a href="/wiki/Peter_Taylor_(footballer,_born_1953)" title="Peter Taylor (footballer, born 1953)">Peter Taylor</a>'s 21-man <a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup_squads#England" title="2013 FIFA U-20 World Cup squads">squad</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2013_FIFA_U-20_World_Cup" title="2013 FIFA U-20 World Cup">2013 FIFA U-20 World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> He made his debut on 16 June, in a 3–0 win in a warm-up match against <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_national_under-20_football_team" title="Uruguay national under-20 football team">Uruguay</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> He assisted <a href="/wiki/Luke_Williams_(footballer,_born_1993)" title="Luke Williams (footballer, born 1993)">Luke Williams</a>' goal in the opening group-stage match on 23 June 2013 against <a href="/wiki/Iraq_national_under-20_football_team" title="Iraq national under-20 football team">Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> He then scored in the following match against <a href="/wiki/Chile_national_under-20_football_team" title="Chile national under-20 football team">Chile</a>, collecting a pass after work by <a href="/wiki/Ross_Barkley" title="Ross Barkley">Ross Barkley</a> and firing in from the edge of the <a href="/wiki/Penalty_area" title="Penalty area">penalty area</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> On 13 August 2013, Kane made his debut for the <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-21_football_team" title="England national under-21 football team">under-21s</a> against <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_under-21_football_team" title="Scotland national under-21 football team">Scotland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FA_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FA-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> In that match, he came on as a substitute in the 58th minute, and England won 6–0.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> On 10 October, he scored a hat-trick for England under-21s against <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_national_under-21_football_team" title="San Marino national under-21 football team">San Marino</a> during <a href="/wiki/2015_UEFA_European_Under-21_Championship_qualification_Group_1" title="2015 UEFA European Under-21 Championship qualification Group 1">2015 UEFA European Under-21 Championship qualification</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Soccerway_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soccerway-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> He continued to score prolifically, with his brace against <a href="/wiki/France_national_under-21_football_team" title="France national under-21 football team">France</a> marking 13 goals in 12 matches for the under-21s.<sup id="cite_ref-Soccerway_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Soccerway-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kane was named in the England under-21 <a href="/wiki/2015_UEFA_European_Under-21_Championship_squads#England" title="2015 UEFA European Under-21 Championship squads">squad</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2015_UEFA_European_Under-21_Championship" title="2015 UEFA European Under-21 Championship">2015 UEFA European Under-21 Championship</a> in the Czech Republic, despite opposition from his club manager <a href="/wiki/Mauricio_Pochettino" title="Mauricio Pochettino">Mauricio Pochettino</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> He played every minute of England's campaign at the tournament, which ended with them eliminated in last place in their group.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Senior">Senior</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:25%; ;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1012376600"/>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">To go out at Wembley and score is what you dream about as a kid. I've had so many good moments this year that it's hard to choose a favourite, but I think that tops them all.</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— Kane speaking about his <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> debut.<sup id="cite_ref-esq_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-esq-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>Kane was also eligible for the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a> through his father, who was born in Galway,<sup id="cite_ref-galway_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-galway-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> but in August 2014 he ruled out switching allegiance, saying that he wanted to break into the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England senior team</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After a good run of form with Tottenham and being the third top goal scorer in the Premier League with 16 goals, on 19 March 2015 Kane was named by manager <a href="/wiki/Roy_Hodgson" title="Roy Hodgson">Roy Hodgson</a> in the England squad to face <a href="/wiki/Lithuania_national_football_team" title="Lithuania national football team">Lithuania</a> in a <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying">UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying</a> match and <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> in a friendly.<sup id="cite_ref-ENG_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ENG-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> He made his international debut at Wembley Stadium, replacing <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Rooney" title="Wayne Rooney">Wayne Rooney</a> in the second half against Lithuania, and scored just 80 seconds later with a header from a <a href="/wiki/Raheem_Sterling" title="Raheem Sterling">Raheem Sterling</a> cross.<sup id="cite_ref-England_4–0_Lithuania_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-England_4–0_Lithuania-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> On 30 March 2015, the day before the Italy match, Hodgson announced that Kane would start alongside Rooney,<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> and he played the full 90 minutes of the 1–1 draw at <a href="/wiki/Juventus_Stadium" title="Juventus Stadium">Juventus Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Laurent_Koscielny_of_France_marking_England_striker_Harry_Kane_(22695724617).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Laurent_Koscielny_of_France_marking_England_striker_Harry_Kane_%2822695724617%29.jpg/220px-Laurent_Koscielny_of_France_marking_England_striker_Harry_Kane_%2822695724617%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="120" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Laurent_Koscielny_of_France_marking_England_striker_Harry_Kane_%2822695724617%29.jpg/330px-Laurent_Koscielny_of_France_marking_England_striker_Harry_Kane_%2822695724617%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Laurent_Koscielny_of_France_marking_England_striker_Harry_Kane_%2822695724617%29.jpg/440px-Laurent_Koscielny_of_France_marking_England_striker_Harry_Kane_%2822695724617%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3502" data-file-height="1907" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Laurent_Koscielny_of_France_marking_England_striker_Harry_Kane_(22695724617).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kane (in white) playing for <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> in 2015. He wears the number 9 jersey for the national team.</div></div></div>
<p>In his next appearance on 5 September 2015, substitute Kane scored the fifth of England's six goals in a win over <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_national_football_team" title="San Marino national football team">San Marino</a> which qualified them for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-San_Marino_0–6_England_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-San_Marino_0–6_England-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> Kane scored his third England goal against <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a> in another qualifier three days later, which they won 2–0.<sup id="cite_ref-England_2–0_Switzerland_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-England_2–0_Switzerland-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> On 12 October 2015, as England finished their qualification campaign with a 10th win from 10 matches, Kane's shot hit the post for an <a href="/wiki/Own_goal" title="Own goal">own goal</a> by Lithuanian goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Giedrius_Arlauskis" title="Giedrius Arlauskis">Giedrius Arlauskis</a> in a 3–0 away victory.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 May 2016, Kane opened the scoring in a 2–1 friendly win over <a href="/wiki/Turkey_national_football_team" title="Turkey national football team">Turkey</a> at the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Manchester_Stadium" title="City of Manchester Stadium">City of Manchester Stadium</a>, but later missed a penalty. He was the first England player to fail to score from the penalty spot during a game since <a href="/wiki/Frank_Lampard" title="Frank Lampard">Frank Lampard</a> in 2010, and the first to miss the target since <a href="/wiki/Peter_Crouch" title="Peter Crouch">Peter Crouch</a> in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-England_2–1_Turkey_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-England_2–1_Turkey-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> At the European Championship in France that June, Kane was assigned to take <a href="/wiki/Corner_kick" title="Corner kick">corner kicks</a>, a tactic which was criticised by pundits,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> but defended by Hodgson, who said that Kane was the best for the role.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
