</p><p>On 10 June 2017, Kane <a href="/wiki/List_of_England_national_football_team_captains" title="List of England national football team captains">captained England</a> for the first time in their <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_F" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification – UEFA Group F">2018 FIFA World Cup qualifier</a> with <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> at <a href="/wiki/Hampden_Park" title="Hampden Park">Hampden Park</a>, scoring an added-time equaliser to rescue a 2–2 draw.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotland_2–2_England_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotland_2–2_England-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> On 5 October, he scored an added-time winner against <a href="/wiki/Slovenia_national_football_team" title="Slovenia national football team">Slovenia</a> which confirmed England's qualification to the 2018 FIFA World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:England_vs_Panama_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/England_vs_Panama_2018.jpg/220px-England_vs_Panama_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/England_vs_Panama_2018.jpg/330px-England_vs_Panama_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/England_vs_Panama_2018.jpg/440px-England_vs_Panama_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:England_vs_Panama_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kane (right) and <a href="/wiki/John_Stones" title="John Stones">John Stones</a> <a href="/wiki/Goal_celebration" title="Goal celebration">celebrating a goal</a> against <a href="/wiki/Panama_national_football_team" title="Panama national football team">Panama</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a></div></div></div>
<p>Kane was named in the 23-man <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_squads#England" title="2018 FIFA World Cup squads">England squad</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup</a> and was made captain.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> On 18 June, Kane scored both of England's goals in a 2–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Tunisia_national_football_team" title="Tunisia national football team">Tunisia</a>, his winning goal coming deep in injury time, in the team's opening group game of the World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> In the next group game on 24 June, Kane scored a <a href="/wiki/List_of_England_national_football_team_hat-tricks" title="List of England national football team hat-tricks">hat-trick in England</a>'s 6–1 win over <a href="/wiki/Panama_national_football_team" title="Panama national football team">Panama</a>, which was England's largest ever World Cup victory.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> With his three goals against Panama, Kane became the third England player to score a hat-trick in a World Cup match, after <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Hurst" title="Geoff Hurst">Geoff Hurst</a> against West Germany in the <a href="/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="1966 FIFA World Cup Final">1966 final</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gary_Lineker" title="Gary Lineker">Gary Lineker</a> against Poland in 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FWC_2018_-_Round_of_16_-_COL_v_ENG_-_Photo_027.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/FWC_2018_-_Round_of_16_-_COL_v_ENG_-_Photo_027.jpg/220px-FWC_2018_-_Round_of_16_-_COL_v_ENG_-_Photo_027.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/FWC_2018_-_Round_of_16_-_COL_v_ENG_-_Photo_027.jpg/330px-FWC_2018_-_Round_of_16_-_COL_v_ENG_-_Photo_027.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/FWC_2018_-_Round_of_16_-_COL_v_ENG_-_Photo_027.jpg/440px-FWC_2018_-_Round_of_16_-_COL_v_ENG_-_Photo_027.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FWC_2018_-_Round_of_16_-_COL_v_ENG_-_Photo_027.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kane (centre) during England's penalty shoot-out win over <a href="/wiki/Colombia_national_football_team" title="Colombia national football team">Colombia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 World Cup</a></div></div></div>
<p>Kane scored his sixth goal of the finals as England overcame <a href="/wiki/Colombia_national_football_team" title="Colombia national football team">Colombia</a> in the Round of 16. Scoring a penalty in a match that finished 1–1 after 120 minutes, also scoring in the penalty shoot-out as England prevailed 4–3; this was the first time that England had managed to win a <a href="/wiki/List_of_FIFA_World_Cup_penalty_shoot-outs" title="List of FIFA World Cup penalty shoot-outs">penalty shoot-out at the World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> Kane didn't score again for the rest of the tournament as England finished in fourth place after losing 2–0 <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a> in the third place playoff.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> However, his six goals in the tournament earned him the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_awards#Golden_Boot" title="FIFA World Cup awards">Golden Boot</a> as the top goalscorer of the World Cup, the first England player to win the award since Gary Lineker became the first to do so in <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">the 1986 tournament</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The September International Break saw the introduction of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Nations_League" title="UEFA Nations League">UEFA Nations League</a>. England's first match was on 8 September 2018 against Spain, which Kane captained for the full 90 minutes in a game which saw England lose 2–1.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> On 15 October England played Spain for the second time in the group, this time running out 3–2 winners with Kane assisting two of the three goals.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> On 14 November, prior to a friendly against the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States men&#39;s national soccer team">United States</a> (US), Kane presented Wayne Rooney with England's Golden Boot in recognition of Rooney's 53 England goals, a record that makes him England's all-time top goal scorer. In an interview following the match, which ended in a 3–0 win for England, Rooney revealed that he wanted Harry Kane to present him the award as he believed that Kane will one day beat it.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> Three days after the US match, Kane captained England in their final Nations League group match against Croatia as the Three Lions won 2–1. Kane first assisted <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Lingard" title="Jesse Lingard">Jesse Lingard</a>'s equaliser then scored the winning goal which saw England top the group and qualify for the finals in June 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2020 qualifying">qualifying round</a> of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020" title="UEFA Euro 2020">UEFA Euro 2020</a>, Kane captained the 1,000th match played by England, and scored a hat-trick against <a href="/wiki/Montenegro_national_football_team" title="Montenegro national football team">Montenegro</a>. This brought his tally to 31, which placed him 6th in the all-time list of England's top goalscorers, but also made him the highest-ever scoring England captain.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> The 7–0 win also secured England's qualification to <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020" title="UEFA Euro 2020">UEFA Euro 2020</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Kane was in fine form throughout the qualifying process, becoming the first Englishman to score in every game in a qualifying campaign, registering a total of twelve goals - the joint-most for an England player in a single year.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_of_play">Style of play</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:25%; ;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1012376600"/>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">I played in different positions as a kid and it helped me learn different parts of the game. Playing alone up front means you have to be good at so much more than taking chances. I know, in a game, I am going to receive the ball with my back to goal, and that the team will need me to link up and bring others into play.</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— Kane on his footballing education, 2016<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div><p>
Kane's former youth coach <a href="/wiki/Alex_Inglethorpe" title="Alex Inglethorpe">Alex Inglethorpe</a> has said of him:</p><blockquote><p>When he first came into the under-18s as a 15 year old, he stood out in the sense he looked a bit gangly. He moved slightly awkwardly, he was a bit cumbersome. But look closer, he had a lot of ability, a great technique. I think he surprised people how good he was. Tactically he was very flexible. He often played in midfield. I remember seeing him once playing as a <a href="/wiki/Midfielder#Holding_midfielder" title="Midfielder">holding midfielder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jim_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jim-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>While a teenager, Kane initially struggled in Tottenham's academy, as partially due to his date of birth in July, he was not as physically developed as other players, nor was he as quick. However, he gained the respect of coaches with his technique and desire for self-improvement.<sup id="cite_ref-jim_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jim-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>When profiling Kane in February 2013, <a href="/wiki/Talksport" title="Talksport">Talksport</a> said that he was best as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Second_striker" title="Forward (association football)">second striker</a>, despite also having ability as a centre forward or in a wide position.<sup id="cite_ref-talksport_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-talksport-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> They wrote that he preferred to place his shots, although he could also score from distance.<sup id="cite_ref-talksport_213-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-talksport-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> The report also noted that he had good pace, but was weak in the air and had not scored on his loan at Norwich.<sup id="cite_ref-talksport_213-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-talksport-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> Initially a back-up to £26&#160;million Spanish import Roberto Soldado and frequently loaned out, Kane was eventually made Tottenham's starting forward by manager Mauricio Pochettino.<sup id="cite_ref-jim_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jim-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Under Pochettino, Kane said that his game has improved through the tough training techniques instituted by the manager.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> He also strives to achieve marginal gain in order to maximise his potential by tweaking various aspects of his training and preparations as well as nutrition.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Analysis">Analysis</span></h3>
<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:25%; ;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1012376600"/>
<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">He seems to have that natural ability to get goals. He's also young, fresh and his attitude appears to be very, very good. What I like about him, is that he is willing to run in behind defenders, as well as go short. When he gets opportunities he inveariably [<i>sic</i>] takes them. He wants to get his shot away very quickly, which is good to see. It looks as if he could have a very good future in the game.</div>
<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">— <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shearer" title="Alan Shearer">Alan Shearer</a>, the Premier League's all-time top scorer, on Kane in March 2015<sup id="cite_ref-shearer_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shearer-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</p>
</div>
<p>Former Tottenham manager <a href="/wiki/David_Pleat" title="David Pleat">David Pleat</a> described Kane as an "old-fashioned traditional centre-forward".<sup id="cite_ref-mcnulty_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcnulty-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Clive_Allen" title="Clive Allen">Clive Allen</a>, who coached him at Tottenham, stated that "one thing I'd say about him, which unfortunately you don't say about a lot of young footballers, is that he had a passion for the game. He loves football, he loves playing, he loves scoring goals".<sup id="cite_ref-mcnulty_217-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcnulty-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> His former Tottenham under-21 coach <a href="/wiki/Les_Ferdinand" title="Les Ferdinand">Les Ferdinand</a> likened Kane's movement to their former forward Teddy Sheringham, and the power and accuracy of his shots to Alan Shearer.<sup id="cite_ref-jim_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jim-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A tall and physical striker,<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> Kane's style of play has been compared to that of former Tottenham forward Jürgen Klinsmann, a comparison Kane called flattering in February 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> In March 2015, <a href="/wiki/Football_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Football Association">Football Association</a> chairman <a href="/wiki/Greg_Dyke" title="Greg Dyke">Greg Dyke</a> named Kane as the benchmark for clubs producing young English players.<sup id="cite_ref-stuff_84-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stuff-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Shearer said that month that the three best strikers playing in the league were Kane, Diego Costa and Sergio Agüero.<sup id="cite_ref-shearer_216-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-shearer-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After Tottenham's victory over Chelsea in January 2015, blogger Chris Miller wrote, "Nobody thought he was the guy who was going to give that performance against Chelsea".<sup id="cite_ref-jim_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jim-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In February 2015, <a href="/wiki/BBC_Sport" title="BBC Sport">BBC Sport</a> wrote that Kane was best as a lone striker, with his "hold-up play and close control" making him apt in other positions as well.<sup id="cite_ref-mcnulty_217-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcnulty-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Also that month, <i><a href="/wiki/Match_of_the_Day" title="Match of the Day">Match of the Day</a></i> pundit <a href="/wiki/Danny_Murphy_(footballer,_born_1977)" title="Danny Murphy (footballer, born 1977)">Danny Murphy</a> said that the England team should be built around Kane, stating, "I'm struggling to see a weakness in the lad's game".<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/ESPN_FC" title="ESPN FC">ESPN</a> reporter Michael Cox stated that "Kane was initially considered a pure goal scorer, he's actually a good all-round player, often playing as an attacking midfielder", pointing out that during the 2018 FIFA World Cup "Kane's contributions in deeper positions were outstanding, his back-to-goal work as impressive as ever".<sup id="cite_ref-ESPN_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ESPN-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> Indeed, although Kane is predominantly known for his clinical finishing and prolific goalscoring ability as an out-and-out striker, he is also known for his vision, technique, link-up play, and passing ability, which enables him to drop deep, bring his teammates into play, and create chances for other players; as such he is also capable of playing in a more creative role as a <a href="/wiki/Forward_(association_football)#Second_striker" title="Forward (association football)">number 10</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> He is also an accurate penalty taker.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span></h3>
<p>However, beginning in 2020, Kane started to be criticised about a perceived tactic of backing into defenders jumping for headers, causing the players to fall backwards onto the pitch, potentially risking serious injury.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> After doing so to Brighton player <a href="/wiki/Adam_Lallana" title="Adam Lallana">Adam Lallana</a> and winning a penalty, Kane was criticised by ex-<a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a> player <a href="/wiki/Martin_Keown" title="Martin Keown">Martin Keown</a> who said, "He looks at his opponent, knows what he is going to do and makes a back for him. I think it is dangerous play from Harry Kane and he knows what he is doing and I don't even think it is a penalty."<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>However, this tactic has been defended by Crystal Palace defender <a href="/wiki/Gary_Cahill" title="Gary Cahill">Gary Cahill</a> who said, "I think that's just part of football. I think an element of that is being clever and experienced and knowing when you can maybe draw a foul in."<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_sponsorship">Media and sponsorship</span></h2>
<p>Kane has a sponsorship deal with sportswear and equipment supplier <a href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc." title="Nike, Inc.">Nike</a>: he wears <a href="/wiki/Nike_Hypervenom" title="Nike Hypervenom">Nike Hypervenom</a> football boots.<sup id="cite_ref-Nike_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nike-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> Following his <a href="/wiki/List_of_Premier_League_players_with_100_or_more_goals" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Premier League players with 100 or more goals">100th Premier League goal</a> in February 2018 Nike launched the special-edition Hypervenom 3 HK.<sup id="cite_ref-Nike_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nike-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> In 2018 he featured in a Nike commercial, 'Nothing Beats A Londoner', along with other sports stars based in the city, including quadruple Olympic champion <a href="/wiki/Mo_Farah" title="Mo Farah">Mo Farah</a> and Chelsea playmaker <a href="/wiki/Eden_Hazard" title="Eden Hazard">Eden Hazard</a>, highlighting London's diversity.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> Ahead of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a>, Kane featured in advertisements for <a href="/wiki/Mars_Bars" class="mw-redirect" title="Mars Bars">Mars Bars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beats_by_Dr._Dre" class="mw-redirect" title="Beats by Dr. Dre">Beats by Dr. Dre</a> headphones, the latter alongside <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Griezmann" title="Antoine Griezmann">Antoine Griezmann</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mario_G%C3%B6tze" title="Mario Götze">Mario Götze</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cesc_F%C3%A0bregas" title="Cesc Fàbregas">Cesc Fàbregas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kane features in <a href="/wiki/EA_Sports" title="EA Sports">EA Sports</a>' <a href="/wiki/FIFA_(video_game_series)" title="FIFA (video game series)"><i>FIFA</i> video game series</a>: he was named in the Team of the Year in <i><a href="/wiki/FIFA_18" title="FIFA 18">FIFA 18</a></i>, joining Lionel Messi and Cristiano Ronaldo in attack.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> Kane and <a href="/wiki/Camila_Cabello" title="Camila Cabello">Camila Cabello</a> announced the winner of the "Best International Male Solo Artist" award at the <a href="/wiki/2018_Brit_Awards" title="2018 Brit Awards">2018 Brit Awards</a> at <a href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena" title="The O2 Arena">the O<sub>2</sub> Arena</a> on 21 February, namely <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 14 May 2020, Kane announced that he will sponsor Leyton Orient's shirts for the next season to help support the first club he played for professionally through the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> The unusual sponsorship deal, the first of its kind in English football, has the approval of <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_Football_League" title="English Football League">English Football League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Football_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Football Association">Football Association</a>, and the sponsorship has been donated to charities which will receive 10% of the proceeds of the respective shirt sales – the home shirt shows a thank you message to the NHS frontline workers tackling the pandemic, the away shirt sporting a logo of Haven House Children's Hospice while the third kit features the mental health charity <a href="/wiki/Mind_(charity)" title="Mind (charity)">Mind</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span></h2>
<p>In an interview given in February 2015, Kane said that he was in a relationship with Katie Goodland, whom he has known since childhood.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> He told <i><a href="/wiki/Esquire_(magazine)" title="Esquire (magazine)">Esquire</a></i> magazine, "We went to school together, so she's seen my whole career. Of course, she's finding it a little crazy. I think she's even been in the papers a couple of times taking the dogs out."<sup id="cite_ref-esq_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-esq-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> On 1 July 2017, Kane announced his engagement to Goodland on his Twitter account,<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> and announced in June 2019 that they had married.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kane and Goodland announced the birth of their first child, Ivy Jane Kane, on 8 January 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> In January 2018, Kane announced that he and Kate were expecting their second child.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> The birth of their second daughter, Vivienne Jane Kane, was announced on 8 August 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> On 18 July 2020, Kane and Goodland announced they were expecting their third child,<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup> two days later revealing in a football-themed gender reveal video that they were expecting a boy.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> Their son, Louis Harry Kane, was born on 29 December 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kane and Goodland have two <a href="/wiki/Labrador_retrievers" class="mw-redirect" title="Labrador retrievers">Labrador retrievers</a>, Brady and Wilson, named after <a href="/wiki/Tom_Brady" title="Tom Brady">Tom Brady</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russell_Wilson" title="Russell Wilson">Russell Wilson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quarterback" title="Quarterback">quarterbacks</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Buccaneers" title="Tampa Bay Buccaneers">Tampa Bay Buccaneers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seattle_Seahawks" title="Seattle Seahawks">Seattle Seahawks</a>, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> Kane has cited <i>The Brady 6</i>, a documentary about Brady, as an inspiration for his development.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> In 2019 Kane expressed an interest in becoming a <a href="/wiki/Placekicker" title="Placekicker">kicker</a> in the NFL "in 10 to 12 years."<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kane abstains from alcohol during the football season, and starting from 2017, he hired a full-time chef to optimise his nutrition.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> He plays <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> in his free time.<sup id="cite_ref-esq_181-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-esq-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Kane was appointed a <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Order_of_the_British_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of the Order of the British Empire">Member of the Order of the British Empire</a> (MBE) in the <a href="/wiki/2019_New_Year_Honours" title="2019 New Year Honours">2019 New Year Honours</a> for services to football.<sup id="cite_ref-MBE_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MBE-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
